## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration depends on position, velocity, and possibly time. The nonlinearity can appear in the restoring force (position-dependent) or damping (velocity-dependent), with possible external time-dependent driving.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 - c1 * x**2) * v + c2 * x (nonlinear damping)
- Forced harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (sinusoidal driving)
- Forced Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Quintic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinearity)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * x**2 (position-dependent damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-cubic damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Combined nonlinear: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v * x**2 (mixed nonlinearities)
- Helmholtz oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 (asymmetric quadratic restoring force)
- Generalized damped: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (full polynomial restoring + damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Symmetric restoring potential → only odd powers of x appear (x, x³, x⁵) in the force expression
- Asymmetric potential (e.g., Helmholtz) → even powers of x (x²) also appear in the restoring force
- Self-sustained oscillations (limit cycles) → velocity-dependent terms with sign changes like (1 - c*x²)*v
- Hardening/softening spring → sign of cubic coefficient x³ determines whether frequency increases/decreases with amplitude
- Autonomous vs non-autonomous → absence of explicit t dependence indicates autonomous system; presence of sin/cos(t) indicates external driving
- Energy-conserving systems → no velocity-dependent terms, force derivable from potential V(x) as -dV/dx
- Nonlinear damping vs linear damping → v*x² or v³ terms indicate amplitude-dependent energy dissipation rate
- Parametric excitation → multiplicative coupling between x and periodic functions of t
